</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Anti-austerity movement in Greece</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=May_2010_Greek_protests&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="May 2010 Greek protests">May 2010 Greek protests</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em;width: 300px">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 125%; background-color: #CEE0F2; vertical-align: middle">Anti-austerity movement in Greece</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #CEE0F2; vertical-align: middle">Part of the <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign_debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign debt crisis">European sovereign debt crisis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_Arab_Spring" title="Impact of the Arab Spring">impact</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a><sup id="cite_ref-Euronews_Greece_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euronews_Greece-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Greek_Revolution_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Greek_Revolution-2">[2]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Causes</th>
<td>Unemployment, inflation, corruption, <a href="/wiki/Greek_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek financial crisis">2010–2011 Greek debt crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> presence in the country, harsh <a href="/wiki/Austerity_measures" class="mw-redirect" title="Austerity measures">austerity measures</a> with welfare cuts, <a href="/wiki/Bipartidism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bipartidism">bipartidism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Particracy" title="Particracy">particracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Democracy deficit">democracy deficit</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Methods</th>
<td>Demonstrations, strike action, <a href="/wiki/Sit-in" title="Sit-in">sit-ins</a>, occupations, rioting, <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assassinations" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassinations">assassinations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Police_violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Police violence">police violence</a>, suicides</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Death(s)</th>
<td>5 May 2010: 3<br />
20 October 2011: 1<br />
4 April 2012&#160;: 1<br />
18 October 2012&#160;: 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Injuries</th>
<td>28–29 June 2011: over 270<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Entasi_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Entasi-3">[3]</a></sup><br />
12 February 2012: over 40<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><br />
5 April 2012&#160;: 1 (Marios Lolos)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>anti-austerity movement</b> in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> involves a series of demonstrations and <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strikes</a> taking place across the country. The events, which began on 5 May 2010, were provoked by plans to cut public spending and raise taxes as <a href="/wiki/Austerity_measure" class="mw-redirect" title="Austerity measure">austerity measures</a> in exchange for a <span class="nowrap">€110 billion</span> bail-out, aimed at solving the <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">Greek government-debt crisis</a>. Three people were killed on 5 May in one of the largest demonstrations in Greece <a href="/wiki/Athens_Polytechnic_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Athens Polytechnic Uprising">since 1973</a>.</p>
<p>On 25&#160;May&#160;2011<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2011-05-25</span>)</span>, anti-austerity activists organised by the <a href="/wiki/Direct_Democracy_Now!" title="Direct Democracy Now!">Direct Democracy Now!</a> movement, known as the <b>Indignant Citizens Movement</b> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Κίνημα Αγανακτισμένων Πολιτών</span>, <i>Kínima Aganaktisménon-Politón</i>), started demonstrating in major cities across Greece. This second wave of demonstrations proved different from the years before<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pandora_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pandora-7">[7]</a></sup> in that they are not partisan<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_xnaria_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_xnaria-8">[8]</a></sup> and began through peaceful means.<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_24_May_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_24_May-9">[9]</a></sup> Some of the events later turned violent, particularly in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-austerity_protests_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-austerity protests in Spain">anti-austerity protests in Spain</a>, these demonstrations were organised entirely using <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_site" class="mw-redirect" title="Social networking site">social networking sites</a>, which earned it the nickname "May of Facebook".<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_27_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_27-14">[14]</a></sup> The demonstrations and square sit-ins were officially ended when municipal police removed demonstrators from <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>'s <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower</a> square on 7 August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 June 2011, violent clashes occurred between the <a href="/wiki/Riot_police" title="Riot police">riot police</a> and activists as the Greek parliament voted to accept the EU's austerity requirements. Incidents of <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> were reported by international media such as the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/CNN_iReport" class="mw-redirect" title="CNN iReport">CNN iReport</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, as well as by academic research<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and organisations <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_police_brutality_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_police_brutality-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_police_brutality_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_police_brutality-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_police_brutality_2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_police_brutality_2-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_police_brutality_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International_police_brutality-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_police_brutality2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International_police_brutality2-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_iReport_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_iReport-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-23">[23]</a></sup> The Athens Prosecutor agreed to an investigation into accusations of excessive use of tear gas, as well as the alleged use of other expired and carcinogenic chemical substances. The investigation is currently under way.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Paremvasi_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Paremvasi-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width: 16em;">

<p><b>Election articles</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_proposed_economy_referendum,_2011" title="Greek proposed economy referendum, 2011">Proposed economy referendum, 2011</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_May_2012" title="Greek legislative election, May 2012">May 2012 election</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_government_formation,_May_2012" title="Greek government formation, May 2012">Government formation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_June_2012" title="Greek legislative election, June 2012">June 2012 election</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_legislative_election,_January_2015" title="Greek legislative election, January 2015">January 2015 election</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_bailout_referendum,_2015" title="Greek bailout referendum, 2015">Greek bailout referendum, 2015</a></li>

<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Greek_economic_crisis" title="Template:Greek economic crisis"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Greek_economic_crisis&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
