<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">Greek government-debt crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greece#2010_debt_crisis" title="Economy of Greece">Economy of Greece &gt; 2010–2011 debt crisis</a></div>
<p>In the early-mid-2000s, the government took advantage of Greece's strong economy by running a large deficit. As the world economy cooled in the late 2000s, Greece was hit hard because its main industries—<a href="/wiki/Greek_Merchant_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Merchant Navy">shipping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Greece" title="Tourism in Greece">tourism</a>—were sensitive to changes in the business cycle. As a result, the country's debt began to pile up rapidly. In early 2010 policy makers<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2011)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> suggested that emergency bailouts might be necessary.</p>
<p>On 5 March 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Hellenic Parliament</a> passed the cost- cutting Economy Protection Bill. On 23 April, the Greek government requested that a bailout package offered by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> be activated.<sup id="cite_ref-bailout_request_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bailout_request-25">[25]</a></sup> The funds were expected to be available quickly, but it was unclear if they would be activated before a crucial 19 May debt rollover. On 27 April, <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">Standard &amp; Poor's</a> cut the country's main debt rating to BB+ ("junk" status), increasing concern that a <a href="/wiki/Default_(finance)" title="Default (finance)">default</a> might occur.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt04282010_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt04282010-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austerity_measures">Austerity measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Austerity measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 May, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou_(junior)" class="mw-redirect" title="George Papandreou (junior)">George Papandreou</a> announced a <a href="/wiki/Third_austerity_package_(Greece)" title="Third austerity package (Greece)">fourth round of austerity measures</a> by the Greek government, described as "unprecedented".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> These include more public sector pay cuts, pension reductions, new taxes on company profits, an increase on luxury and <a href="/wiki/Sin_tax" title="Sin tax">sin taxes</a>, and an increase of the <a href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value added tax">value added tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The proposed changes, which aim to save <span class="nowrap">€30 billion</span> through 2012, represent the biggest government overhaul within a single generation.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup> The cuts are in line with the EU-<a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> loan proposals, which demand that Greece liberalise its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> They helped Greece reach a loan agreement, announced on 2 May, for an immediate <span class="nowrap">€45 billion</span> in loans (with a 5% interest for the most part, provided by the EU), with additional funds available in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-businessweek20100305_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek20100305-35">[35]</a></sup> The total value of the loans was expected to be in the <span class="nowrap">€110 billion</span> range.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> Papandreou submitted the bill to Parliament on 4 May.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Hellenic Parliament was expected to vote on the proposed austerity measures on 6 May.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a>, the conservative minority party, vowed to vote against the bill, but the bill was expected to pass because of the <a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a>'s large 160-seat advantage in Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> The government has pleaded with demoralised staff not to retire, fearing that a surge in benefits requests could further drain the public treasury.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In separate votes on 29 and 30 June, Parliament approved the austerity measures.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_to_the_2008_Greek_riots">Relationship to the 2008 Greek riots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Relationship to the 2008 Greek riots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2008_Greek_riots" title="2008 Greek riots">2008 Greek riots</a> started on 6 December 2008, when Alexandros Grigoropoulos (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Αλέξανδρος Γρηγορόπουλος</span>), a 15-year-old student, was killed by two policemen<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Exarcheia" title="Exarcheia">Exarcheia</a> district of central <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. While the unrest was triggered by the shooting incident, commentators<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> described the reactions as expressing deeper causes, especially a widespread feeling of frustration in the younger generation about the economic problems of the country (partly as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_crisis_of_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic crisis of 2008">global economic crisis</a>), a rising unemployment rate among young people and a perception of general inefficiency and corruption in Greek state institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-displaystory1_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-displaystory1-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-international1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international1-45">[45]</a></sup> Related sporadic protests have continued into 2011.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_protests">2010 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2010 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_5_May_2010">Before 5 May 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Before 5 May 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On May Day, there were protest marches in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, by many unions, left-wing, anarchist and communist party supporters. Violent clashes broke out when riot police were sent out to contain the protestors.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_may_day_rallies_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_may_day_rallies-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 May, members of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party of Greece</a> broke into the <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Athens" title="Acropolis of Athens">Acropolis of Athens</a> and hung banners: "Peoples of Europe Rise Up".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="5_May_2010_strike_and_demonstrations">5 May 2010 strike and demonstrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 5 May 2010 strike and demonstrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In response to the proposed spending cuts and tax increases, a nationwide strike was called for 5 May. Starting at midnight, aeroplane, train, and ferry traffic in and out of the country ceased.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> Schools, some hospitals, and many private businesses were closed.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> The demonstrations are seen by some as the most widespread since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%931974" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek military junta of 1967–1974">Greek military junta of 1967–1974</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-burns_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burns-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>An estimated 100,000 people marched through Athens,<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-burns_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burns-48">[48]</a></sup> with some estimates stretching to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-turnout_5_may_rallies_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turnout_5_may_rallies-49">[49]</a></sup> As protests gained momentum, a large group tried to storm the parliament building in <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a> in Athens, where they scuffled with police, causing some of the <a href="/wiki/Evzones" title="Evzones">Evzones</a> (ceremonial guards) to flee from the <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier" title="Tomb of the Unknown Soldier">Tomb of the Unknown Soldier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-burns_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burns-48">[48]</a></sup> The protesters accused members of parliament of being "thieves".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> Riot police were able to push the crowds back with <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flash_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Flash bomb">flash bombs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smoke_bomb" title="Smoke bomb">smoke bombs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> Nearby buildings, including a finance ministry building, were set on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> Prime Minister George Papandreou responded "Nobody has the right to violence and particularly violence that leads to murder. Violence breeds violence."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Outside_MARFIN_bank.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Outside_MARFIN_bank.png/220px-Outside_MARFIN_bank.png" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Outside_MARFIN_bank.png/330px-Outside_MARFIN_bank.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Outside_MARFIN_bank.png/440px-Outside_MARFIN_bank.png 2x" data-file-width="473" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Outside_MARFIN_bank.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
People paying their respects to the memory of the people who died on 5 May.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Protesters set fire to a <a href="/wiki/Marfin_Investment_Group" title="Marfin Investment Group">Marfin Bank</a> branch on <a href="/wiki/Stadiou_Street" title="Stadiou Street">Stadiou Street</a> with <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktails</a>; witnesses said that protestors marching past the bank ignored the employees' cries for help, while others chanted <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a> slogans.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kathimerini_protest_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathimerini_protest-50">[50]</a></sup> Most of the bank's employees managed to escape the burning building, but two employees who jumped from the second-story balcony were injured and two women and a man were found dead after the fire was extinguished.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerdos_protest_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerdos_protest-51">[51]</a></sup> It was reported that fire crews had difficulty reaching the scene because of demonstrations moving through the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathimerini_protest_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathimerini_protest-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbs_newshour_interview_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbs_newshour_interview-52">[52]</a></sup> The victims died of <a href="/wiki/Asphyxiation" class="mw-redirect" title="Asphyxiation">asphyxiation</a> from toxic fumes when they were unable to escape from a roof exit that was blocked. They had gone to work despite the general strike over fears of losing their jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> They have been identified as Paraskevi Zoulia, 35, Angeliki Papathanasopoulou, 32 (who was four months pregnant), and Epaminondas Tsakalis, 36.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Papandreou called the incident a "murderous act".<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michalis_Chrysohoidis" class="mw-redirect" title="Michalis Chrysohoidis">Michalis Chrysohoidis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_the_Protection_of_the_Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for the Protection of the Citizen">Minister for the Protection of the Citizen</a>, declared that "today is a black day for democracy ... undemocratic forces have [latched on to] a peaceful demonstration of workers and now petrol bombs have killed three of our citizens and put an immediate danger to the lives of others."<sup id="cite_ref-Kerdos_protest_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerdos_protest-51">[51]</a></sup> He also stated that "the killers will be caught and punished accordingly". Police started a widespread search, with the help of closed-circuit television footage to detect and arrest the suspects. The police blamed "hooded youth" for the incident,<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> while one protestor who spoke to BBC blamed police brutality for the escalation of violence which was started when protestors threw <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktails</a> at police; the police responded with pepper spray and tear gas.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> In response to the incident, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greek_Federation_of_Bank_Employees%27_Unions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Greek Federation of Bank Employees' Unions (page does not exist)">Greek Federation of Bank Employees' Unions</a> blamed bank management for inadequate safety measures in the building and called for strike action.<sup id="cite_ref-bank_employees_strike_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bank_employees_strike-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Elsewhere in Athens, some demonstrators threw rocks, bottles, and pieces of marble at the police.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> Numerous trash bins were lit on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> Some broke windows, threw petrol bombs, and committed other acts of vandalism.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_protest_37-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_protest-37">[37]</a></sup> Other protesters set up barricades and burned cars.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup> Across Athens, at least 12 people were injured,<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_Sun_protest_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Sun_protest-56">[56]</a></sup> and more than 70 people were detained for questioning.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, 37 people were arrested as a result of the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Herald_Sun_protest_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herald_Sun_protest-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath_of_protest_of_5_May">Aftermath of protest of 5 May</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Aftermath of protest of 5 May">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 5 and 6 May 2010, the Hellenic Parliament passed the proposed austerity measures, claiming they show the Greek government's commitment to tackling its <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a>, amongst continued protests.<sup id="cite_ref-businessweek20100305_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek20100305-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also on 5 May, the German parliament began debating the bailout package, as Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> urged rapid passage.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> Merkel remarked that "Quite simply, Europe's future is at stake."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> The plan requires Germany to provide the largest share, <span class="nowrap">€22 billion</span>, of the bailout funds.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup> The plan must be approved by 15 <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> countries in total.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_protest_36-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_protest-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Analysts said the protests could mark the beginning of protracted <a href="/wiki/Social_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="Social unrest">social unrest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup> If that occurs, the country could be pushed into deep recession.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup> Economists have warned that it could be ten years before the Greek economy recovers, even if it does not worsen first.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_protest_31-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_protest-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>There has been advocacy for a <a href="/wiki/Political_coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Political coalition">political coalition</a> from within the Greek political elite, and by the Greek journalist <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Papahelas" title="Alexis Papahelas">Alexis Papahelas</a> who said that Papandreou should 'get rid of some of the novices he has in his government, make an overture to the opposition and go full-steam ahead.'<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>One columnist at <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a> suggests in an editorial that the protests speak of a deeper issue in Greek politics: she asks, 'What the advocates of this scenario [coalition government] do not seem to grasp is that the political class is out of touch with the population,' and 'How can we expect to see solutions and progress by the very same people who are inextricably, causally linked to the problem?'<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However other sources <sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>suggest that the movement was a positive reaction triggering a series of innovative socio-political processes.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_of_the_2011_protests">Background of the 2011 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Background of the 2011 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg/220px-Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg.png" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg/330px-Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg/440px-Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="724" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greece_public_debt_1999-2010.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first round of austerity in 2010 failed to stop Greece's rising debt, which is expected to go up by 10% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-To_Vima_predictions_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-To_Vima_predictions-62">[62]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2010_European_sovereign_debt_crisis#Greek_government_funding_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 European sovereign debt crisis">Greek Government funding crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greece#2010_debt_crisis" title="Economy of Greece">Economy of Greece &gt; 2010–2011 debt crisis</a></div>
<p>The memorandum signed between Greece and the IMF became largely unpopular in Greece, with some polls showing that 62% believe it was a bad decision. This memorandum came into action 7 October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue-63">[63]</a></sup> Amid accusations that the government has not achieved its goals according to the IMF memorandum, some countries in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> have stated that they will not be lending Greece any more money if the IMF does not do so, including the Netherlands, Germany and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_3_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_3-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_28_3_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_28_3-65">[65]</a></sup> Some European officials went so far as to say that Greece should start selling away its assets to other European nations to receive loans, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> Minister of Finance said that the Greek parliament would not like this proposal and characterised the opinion of the Greek parliament as "a sensibility" that no one can consider at this time.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_28_3_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_28_3-65">[65]</a></sup> Meanwhile, unemployment exceeded 15%, while a large percentage of full-time workers only receive the minimum wage of 592 Euros, or less.<sup id="cite_ref-in.gr_minimum_wage_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-in.gr_minimum_wage-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-imerisia_unemployment_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imerisia_unemployment-67">[67]</a></sup> Rumours in regards to Greece's exclusion from the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> also added to frustration, but these were categorically rejected by the Greek government, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Greece" title="Bank of Greece">Bank of Greece</a> and IMF-director nominee, and French Finance Minister, <a href="/wiki/Christine_Lagarde" title="Christine Lagarde">Christine Lagarde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_1-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_27_1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_27_1-69">[69]</a></sup> On 29 June 2011, amid violent protests, the second austerity package was passed with 155 votes in favour in the 300-seat parliament. The next day, the Office of the <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="High Commissioner for Human Rights">High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> of the United Nations reported an independent UN expert's warning that the austerity measures could result in violations of the Greek people's human rights, such as "rights to food, water, adequate housing and work under fair and equitable conditions".<sup id="cite_ref-UN_human_rights_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_human_rights-70">[70]</a></sup> Meanwhile, other international media have questioned the necessity of a second austerity package, when the first one brought in no results.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_austerity_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_austerity-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Greece signed the Memorandum with the European Union and the IMF in 2010, the matter of the constitutional legality of the memorandum came under criticism in Greece, both by the people and some of the country's most prominent university professors of law.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_constitution_1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_constitution_1-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_constitution_2_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_constitution_2-73">[73]</a></sup> The Athens Association of Lawyers, as well as a number of labour unions, brought the question of the legality of the memorandum to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Greece)" title="Council of State (Greece)">Council of State</a> of the Greek government, but the Council judged the contract to be constitutional in late June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_mnimonio_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_mnimonio-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Council_of_State_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Council_of_State-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Apart from the economic crisis, there is also a developing political crisis in the country. The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> asked the major parties in Greece to come to an agreement in regards to the new set of austerity measures, but twice the major parties failed.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_27_2_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_27_2-76">[76]</a></sup> In a poll published on 29 May 2011, the two major parties (the ruling <a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> and the main opposition <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a>) gathered slightly under 40% of the total number of votes, with the ruling party having 19%, while the opposition came first with 19.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_dikomatismos_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_dikomatismos-77">[77]</a></sup> In another poll published the same day, the ruling party came first with 20.7% while the opposition came second with 20.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_dikomatismos_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_dikomatismos-77">[77]</a></sup> According to the polls, neither of the two parties could form a government, even if they combined forces.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The lack of co-ordination within the government (with conflicting government officials stating opposite 'government positions') also fuelled the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_thema_paraplanitika_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_thema_paraplanitika-78">[78]</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Maria_Damanaki" title="Maria Damanaki">Maria Damanaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Maritime_Affairs_and_Fisheries" title="European Commissioner for Maritime Affairs and Fisheries">European Commissioner for Maritime Affairs and Fisheries</a>, stated that "our withdrawal from the Eurozone is on the table, we have to speak frankly" on 25 May,<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_damanaki_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_damanaki-79">[79]</a></sup> Greek banks lost liquidity equal to 1.5&#160;billion Euro from withdrawals in two days.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_thema_paraplanitika_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_thema_paraplanitika-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mish_30_May_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mish_30_May-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_1.5_dis_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_1.5_dis-81">[81]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Minister of Finance, <a href="/wiki/Giorgos_Papakonstantinou" title="Giorgos Papakonstantinou">Giorgos Papakonstantinou</a>, vehemently denied that exiting the Eurozone is being considered.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_thema_paraplanitika_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_thema_paraplanitika-78">[78]</a></sup> On 1 June, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Orthodox_Rally" title="Popular Orthodox Rally">Popular Orthodox Rally</a> party, <a href="/wiki/Georgios_Karatzaferis" title="Georgios Karatzaferis">Georgios Karatzaferis</a>, announced that his party is considering resigning from parliament, thus causing the dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Hellenic Parliament</a> and triggering national elections.<sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_Karatzaferis_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_Karatzaferis-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Karatzaferis_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Karatzaferis-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Karatzaferis_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Karatzaferis-84">[84]</a></sup> He also commented that "I see a Prime Minister that is unable to react, an opposition that is unwilling to play the game, and a <a href="/wiki/Left_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Left (politics)">Left</a> that is in its own little world".<sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_Karatzaferis_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_Karatzaferis-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Karatzaferis_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Karatzaferis-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_protests">2011 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2011 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February_2011">February 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: February 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 23 February 2011, there was a recurrence of violent protests and strikes, involving up to 100,000 people<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> as German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> called for a renewal of the loan programme to Greece<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> that had been conditioned on fiscal tightening. The measures adopted by Greece were considered harsh by the protesters.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22Indignant_Citizens_Movement.22_.28May.E2.80.93August.29">The "Indignant Citizens Movement" (May–August)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The &quot;Indignant Citizens Movement&quot; (May–August)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="May">May</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: May">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png/220px-Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png/330px-Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png/440px-Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="473" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Syntagma_Square_%27indignados%27.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Demonstrators in the plaza in front of the Greek parliament, 25 May.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png/220px-Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png/330px-Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png/440px-Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png 2x" data-file-width="632" data-file-height="471" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Real_Democracy_Now_information_kiosk.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Real_Democracy_Now!_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Democracy Now! (Greece)">Real Democracy Now!</a> information kiosk at Syntagma Square, 31 May.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 25 May 2011, there is a peaceful demonstration in Athens and other major cities, protesting the new austerity measures proposed by the government, in the same spirit as the <a href="/wiki/2011_Spanish_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Spanish protests">2011 Spanish protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_xnaria_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_xnaria-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup> The demonstrations include most major Greek cities:<a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larissa" title="Larissa">Larissa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patras" title="Patras">Patras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volos" title="Volos">Volos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rethymno" title="Rethymno">Rethymno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripoli_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripoli (Greece)">Tripoli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalamata" title="Kalamata">Kalamata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ERT_1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERT_1-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_poleis_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_poleis-91">[91]</a></sup> The demonstration in Athens is coordinated by the Facebook page "Αγανακτισμένοι Στο Σύνταγμα" (Indignants at <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Facebook_Athens_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facebook_Athens-92">[92]</a></sup> Currently, it is reported that over 90,000 people have registered on the page,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and thousands (reportedly over 30,000)<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_xnaria_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_xnaria-8">[8]</a></sup> have gathered outside the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Greek Parliament</a> in Syntagma square.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The demonstration in Greece's second-largest city, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, is co-ordinated by the Facebook page "Αγανακτισμένοι στον Λευκό Πύργο" (Indignants at the <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower</a>), and over 35,000 people have said they would 'attend' the protest.<sup id="cite_ref-Facebook_Thessaloniki_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facebook_Thessaloniki-96">[96]</a></sup> Some of the most popular slogans at protest on 25 May were:</p>
<ul>
<li>Error 404, Democracy was not found.<sup id="cite_ref-s1_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>I vote, You vote, He votes, She votes, We vote, You vote, They steal.</li>
<li>Greece your turn has come, you have to stop burying your children.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_polites_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_polites-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oust! (Greek interjection of a negative nature, meaning "leave")</li>
<li>The maid resisted. What do we do? (Reference to <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Strauss-Kahn_sexual_assault_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominique Strauss-Kahn sexual assault case">an alleged sex scandal</a> involving former IMF director <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Strauss-Kahn" title="Dominique Strauss-Kahn">Dominique Strauss-Kahn</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>This series of demonstrations differed from almost all other demonstrations in Greece's <a href="/wiki/Metapolitefsi" title="Metapolitefsi">metapolitefsi</a> era (1975–present) in that it was a protest organised without political or trade union affiliations.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup> Demonstrators who expressed political party affiliation during the demonstrations were condemned by the majority of the demonstrators, as the organizers claimed that there was no room for political affiliation or violence in the demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-ERT_1_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERT_1-89">[89]</a></sup> The focus of the protesters was against the government and the current driving forces of <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Greece" title="Politics of Greece">Greek politics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup> As a response to the Spanish slogan "Be quiet, the Greeks are sleeping" (which was allegedly heard at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Spanish_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Spanish protests">2011 Spanish protests</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_25_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_25-99">[99]</a></sup> a big banner was raised in front of the Spanish embassy in Athens reading "¡Estamos despiertos! ¿Que hora es? ¡Ya es hora de que se vayan!" (We've woken up! What time is it? Its time they left!).<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-E-TYPOS_vroxi_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E-TYPOS_vroxi-100">[100]</a></sup> There was also a strong sense of disapproval for the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Greece" title="Prime Minister of Greece">Prime Minister of Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">George Papandreou</a>, and the vice-president of the government, <a href="/wiki/Theodoros_Pangalos_(politician)" title="Theodoros Pangalos (politician)">Theodoros Pangalos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_orgi_88-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_orgi-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_26_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_26-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The demonstrations continued nationwide for a second day on 26 May.<sup id="cite_ref-E-TYPOS_vroxi_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E-TYPOS_vroxi-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_2_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_2-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_live_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_live-103">[103]</a></sup> Despite heavy rainfall in central Athens, reportedly over 14,000, people<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_26_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_26-101">[101]</a></sup> gathered in front of the Greek parliament for a second day in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_video_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_video-104">[104]</a></sup> The media reported that half of the people gathered at Syntagma Square in Athens were youth, whereas the other half were over 40, including families and children.<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_video_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_video-104">[104]</a></sup> In line with the Spanish quote of "Be quiet, the Greeks are sleeping" which triggered the Greek protests, two new banners appeared, one in French (Silence! Les Français dorment! Ils revent de '68, <i>Silence! The French are sleeping! They are dreaming of (May) '68</i>) and one in Italian (Zitti che svegliamo gli Italiani... <i>Be quiet, you will wake up the Italians...</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_video_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_video-104">[104]</a></sup> An information center and a "book of ideas" have also been set up at Syntagma Square.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27-105">[105]</a></sup> Additionally, a number of people were banging pots and pans.<sup id="cite_ref-SKAI_video_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SKAI_video-104">[104]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, Greece's second city and second-largest center of demonstrations, the protesters hung a huge For Sale sign from the city's main landmark, the <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower</a>, as a protest against the government's massive denationalisation schedule, which they perceived as "selling away our country's assets".<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_27_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_27-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_27_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_27-107">[107]</a></sup> Although the demonstrations in Thessaloniki were visibly smaller on 26 May, with around 2,500 people participating, competing with a major football game between the city's two major teams and the shops and markets open until late that evening.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27-105">[105]</a></sup> Some people set up encampments.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_27_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_27-106">[106]</a></sup> In Thessaloniki's protests there was much more of a sense of direct democracy, as citizens were free to take the floor and speak, voice their concerns and opinions, and contribute ideas about what should be done next, receiving the full attention of the other demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_27_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_27-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_27_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_27-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_26_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_26-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg/220px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg.png" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg/330px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg/440px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1052" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_Syntagma_Square.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first vote of the people's assembly of Syntagma Square.<sup id="cite_ref-Real_Democracy_Now.21_vote_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Democracy_Now.21_vote-109">[109]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Demonstrations continued for a third consecutive day on 27 May.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_27_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_27-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_27_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_27-111">[111]</a></sup> Thousands of people gathered in front of the Greek parliament, again in heavy downpour, joined by the "I'm Not Paying" movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_27_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_27-110">[110]</a></sup> As a means of protesting, people wearing white masks formed a human shield around the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, in Syntagma Square.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_27_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_27-110">[110]</a></sup> The demonstrations continued peacefully, and when one protester shouted a slogan against the police, he was heavily condemned by other demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_27_110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_27-110">[110]</a></sup> On 27 May, the proceedings of the first <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">people's assembly</a> on Syntagma Square were published by the <a href="/wiki/Real_Democracy_Now!_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Democracy Now! (Greece)">Real Democracy Now!</a> movement. Among them:<sup id="cite_ref-Proceedings_27_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proceedings_27-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Any corrupt politician should either be sent home or to jail.</li>
<li>When we, the people, start discussions without fear, fear grips them, inside the parliament building.</li>
<li>This is not just the politician's fault. It's all our faults, with our selfish attitudes.</li>
<li>Demonstrations should take place every evening at 6&#160;pm and an <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">assembly</a> at 9&#160;pm.</li>
<li>Their democracy guarantees neither Justice nor Equality.</li>
<li>The taxation system is not the same for the rich and the poor. Equal rights for everyone.</li>
</ul>
<p>On 28 May, demonstrations continued with at least 7,000 people gathered in front of the Greek parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Star_28_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star_28-113">[113]</a></sup> A number of new flags appeared, including those of Tunisia, Argentina, Armenia and Hungary. At least 20 people set up tents in the square.<sup id="cite_ref-Star_28_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star_28-113">[113]</a></sup> Major demonstrations also took place in Thessaloniki, Patras and Heraklion.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_28_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_28-114">[114]</a></sup> In Thessaloniki a cycling race was organised as part of the demonstration.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_28_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_28-115">[115]</a></sup> All across the country the movement was becoming more organised, media reported, with teams of doctors, translators, and food supplies set up by the protesters, especially at Syntagma Square, which had turned into the main protest center for the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_28_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_28-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg/220px-2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg/330px-2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg/440px-2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="461" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_Greece_Uprising.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Demonstrators in front of the Greek parliament, 29 May.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>29 May was set as a day of peaceful pan-European demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-Facebook_Europe_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facebook_Europe-116">[116]</a></sup> It was estimated that the demonstration in Athens alone attracted more than 100,000 demonstrators in front of the Greek parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_100.2C000_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_100.2C000-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_100.2C000_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_100.2C000-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_100.2C000_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_100.2C000-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Euronews_100.2C000_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euronews_100.2C000-120">[120]</a></sup> while others put the estimates around 80,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_6i_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_6i-121">[121]</a></sup> Demonstrations included people of all ages and financial backgrounds. The oldest person at the demonstration was a 102-year-old grandmother looking after her granddaughter, who also spoke at the <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">people's assembly</a> in support of the demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_102_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_102-122">[122]</a></sup> An estimated 10,000 people gathered in front of the <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower of Thessaloniki</a> in Greece's second city, and demonstrations were also held in many other Greek cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_30_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_30-123">[123]</a></sup> Some of the most popular slogans that were heard on 29 May were "the worst form of violence is poverty" and "a magical night, like in Argentina, lets see who gets in the helicopter first!", a reference to <a href="/wiki/President_of_Argentina" title="President of Argentina">Argentine President</a> <a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_la_R%C3%BAa" title="Fernando de la Rúa">Fernando de la Rúa</a>'s resignation and escape from the presidential mansion using a helicopter in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_102_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_102-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_30_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_30-123">[123]</a></sup> Some of the demands that the <a href="/wiki/Real_Democracy_Now!_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Democracy Now! (Greece)">Real Democracy Now!</a> movement has formulated during the <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">assemblies</a> at syntagma Square include:<sup id="cite_ref-Real_Democracy_Now.21_demands_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Democracy_Now.21_demands-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Adoption of a new constitution, written by the people and not the members of parliament</li>
<li>Refusal to pay debt which members of the movement consider to be <a href="/wiki/Odious_debt" title="Odious debt">odious</a></li>
<li>Cancellation of the memorandum signed between Greece and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a></li>
<li>Harder taxation on the rich.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg/220px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg.png" width="220" height="364" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg/330px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg/440px-Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vote_of_the_People%27s_Assembly_of_the_White_Tower_Square.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A similar vote was issued by the people's assembly in Thessaloniki.<sup id="cite_ref-Indignants_of_Thessaloniki_vote_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indignants_of_Thessaloniki_vote-125">[125]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>30 May saw continued demonstrations in Athens and other cities around Greece, although visibly smaller than the demonstrations of 29 May.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_6i_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_6i-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_30_2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_30_2-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_31_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_31-127">[127]</a></sup> More than 4,000 people demonstrated in front of the Greek parliament on 30 May,<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_30_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_30-128">[128]</a></sup> with some sources claiming that over 10,000 people were present.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31-129">[129]</a></sup> The demonstrators also set up a set of <a href="/wiki/Gallow" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallow">gallows</a> in front of the parliament, demanding that those responsible for the crisis be sent to justice.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31-129">[129]</a></sup> Over 30 tents were set up in front of the <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower of Thessaloniki</a> in Greece's second-largest city, where a direct democracy style <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">people's assembly</a> took place every evening.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_30_2_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_30_2-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>31 May marked seven days since the start of the protests, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Athens" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Athens">University of Athens</a> hosted an anti-government protest with the aid of famous Greek composer and anti-dictatorship fighter <a href="/wiki/Mikis_Theodorakis" title="Mikis Theodorakis">Mikis Theodorakis</a>, while the dean of the University was also a key speaker at the event.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31-129">[129]</a></sup> Once the protest at the university was over, the 10,000 protesters joined forces with the demonstrators already in front of the parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_2_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31_2-130">[130]</a></sup> totalling between 25,000 and 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_2_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31_2-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_31_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_31-131">[131]</a></sup> The demonstrators surrounded the Greek parliament, making it impossible for MPs and workers inside the building to exit.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_2_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31_2-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_31_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_31-131">[131]</a></sup> while Eight MPs escaped through the adjacent National Gardens.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_31_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_31-131">[131]</a></sup> Later, riot police created a passage to enable MPs to exit the parliament, to the loud condemnation of 1,000 protesters gathered at the side entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_31_3_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_31_3-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="June">June</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: June">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Demonstrations continued on 1 June. At <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, protesters surrounded a restaurant where Greek and foreign members of parliament were having a dinner, shouting slogans against them while a few were throwing rocks and other objects at the politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Kerkyra_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Kerkyra-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Kerkyra_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Kerkyra-135">[135]</a></sup> Finally, the officials were forced to escape using a boat, as the restaurant was near the harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Kerkyra_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Kerkyra-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Kerkyra_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Kerkyra-135">[135]</a></sup> In Athens, more than 15,000 people gathered in front of the parliament to protest for an eighth day in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> This time they were also joined by the <i>Society for the Protection of Citizens by the Arbitration of Banks</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> and also a group of motorcyclists who also showed their support for the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> Earlier that evening the riot police had closed up the streets leading up to the embassy of Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> To avoid being blockaded inside the parliament like on 31 May, the members of parliament left early on 1 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> Among thousands of protesters in Syntagma square, 32 Greek scientists addressed a letter to the members of parliament calling them to announce the whole truth of the situation<sup id="cite_ref-Zougla.gr_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zougla.gr-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets,_day_22.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png/220px-Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png/330px-Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png/440px-Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets%2C_day_22.png 2x" data-file-width="635" data-file-height="476" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_indignants_cleaning_streets,_day_22.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Indignants cleaning the streets around Syntagma Square on their 22nd day of protest on 15 June.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>5 June was set as a second day of pan-European demonstrations and marked the 12th continuous day of demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra_133-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Kerkyra-133">[133]</a></sup> It is estimated that well over 200,000 gathered at Athens' <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a> that evening to protest against the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_5_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_5-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_5_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_5-138">[138]</a></sup> Some sources put the number of people in front of the parliament to over 300,000<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_5_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_5-139">[139]</a></sup> while the organizers claim that over 500,000 people took part in the demonstration,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_5_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_5-137">[137]</a></sup> making it the largest demonstration in Athens since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Popular_assembly" title="Popular assembly">people's assembly</a> a direct connection with <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol" title="Puerta del Sol">Puerta del Sol</a> was made via <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_5_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_5-139">[139]</a></sup> Some tension occurred on 5 June, as protesters were prevented from heading towards <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a> by riot police,<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_5_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_5-139">[139]</a></sup> which had put together large metallic barriers to close off streets.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_5_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_5-138">[138]</a></sup> Police also brought a <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a> to the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_5_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_5-138">[138]</a></sup> Demonstrations also took place in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patras" title="Patras">Patras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heraklion" title="Heraklion">Heraklion</a>, as well as many other Greek cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_5_138-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_5-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_5_139-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_5-139">[139]</a></sup> Some of the most popular slogans of that day included:<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_5_138-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_5-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Bread-Education-Freedom – the dictatorship didn't fall in '73!</li>
<li>We do not owe, we will not sell away, we will not pay.</li>
<li>Minister of culture, minister of censorship<sup id="cite_ref-s1_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s1-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:June_29_Athens_street_fire.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/June_29_Athens_street_fire.png/220px-June_29_Athens_street_fire.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/June_29_Athens_street_fire.png/330px-June_29_Athens_street_fire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/June_29_Athens_street_fire.png/440px-June_29_Athens_street_fire.png 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="475" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:June_29_Athens_street_fire.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A bin on fire during riots of 29 June in a street near parliament.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg/220px-20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg/330px-20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg/440px-20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20110629_Old_man_hit_by_Riot_Police_in_demonstrations_in_Athens_Greece.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Clash between riot police and a citizen – 29 June 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Demonstrations continued throughout June, both at <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a> and other squares in cities across the country. On 28 June 2011, Greek unions, including those whose members dominate the country's health, transportation, education, and government jobs began a 48-hour strike, in protest of the deteriorating economic situation and suggestions on the part of the government of new austerity measures.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz-141">[141]</a></sup> The walkout led to the freezing of a number of public services.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz-141">[141]</a></sup> Journalists and a number of artists also stopped working in solidarity with the protest.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz-141">[141]</a></sup> That day demonstrations turned violent as protestors clashed with police in front of the Greek parliament and other areas of central <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Entasi_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Entasi-3">[3]</a></sup> Violence continued during the night and on 29 June, the day when a new package of deeply unpopular austerity measures was passed.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Greece_crisis_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Greece_crisis-142">[142]</a></sup> The police attempted to evacuate Syntagma Square of protesters, as well as other key protest points in Athens, by driving through the crowds on motorbikes and throwing stun grenades while making extensive use of tear gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_June_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_June-143">[143]</a></sup> Media also mention that the police used unnecessary violence against protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_June_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_June-143">[143]</a></sup> Officials from the <a href="/wiki/Athens_Metro" title="Athens Metro">Athens Metro</a> also said that the police had fired <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> inside the Syntagma Square metro station.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_police_brutality_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_police_brutality-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_June_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_June-143">[143]</a></sup> Police also stormed <a href="/wiki/Monastiraki" title="Monastiraki">Monastiraki</a>, as well as the streets around the <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Athens" title="Acropolis of Athens">Acropolis</a>, randomly hitting people eating at taverns and making extensive use of chemicals and stun grenades.<sup id="cite_ref-Dalakoglou_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dalakoglou-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TVXS.gr_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVXS.gr-145">[145]</a></sup> Doctors at the infirmary set up at Othonos Square said the police had attacked them using stones and pieces of marble.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_June_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_June-143">[143]</a></sup> Earlier, two members of the Teacher's Association were attacked by police and were injured, one of them on the head.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Entasi_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Entasi-3">[3]</a></sup> Police also tried to deny access to the square to an ambulance attempting to transport heavily injured civilians to a hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_June_143-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_June-143">[143]</a></sup> A total of about 270 people were injured on 28 June alone, and over 500 visited the Syntagma Square metro station infirmary on 29 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Entasi_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Entasi-3">[3]</a></sup> The Ministry of Health reported that 99 people were sent to hospitals on 29 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Ageliofiros_29_June_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ageliofiros_29_June-146">[146]</a></sup> Following almost two days of violence in the streets in front of the Greek parliament, the Greek TV channel <a href="/wiki/Alter_Channel" title="Alter Channel">Alter</a> aired a video with claiming that it was showing members of the <a href="/wiki/Riot_police" title="Riot police">riot police</a> co-operating with extreme Right syndicalists.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ERT_MAT_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERT_MAT-148">[148]</a></sup> The Minister for Citizen Protection, <a href="/wiki/Christos_Papoutsis" title="Christos Papoutsis">Christos Papoutsis</a>, ordered an immediate investigation in the claims<sup id="cite_ref-YPP_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YPP-149">[149]</a></sup> according to which the police collaborrated with hooded neo-Nazis .<sup id="cite_ref-ERT_MAT_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERT_MAT-148">[148]</a></sup> The damage caused to Athens' historic city center is estimated to be over 500,000 euro,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Zimia_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Zimia-150">[150]</a></sup> as shop fronts were vandalised by hooded youth.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_30_June_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_30_June-151">[151]</a></sup> Finally, it had been proved that there was no cooperation between Greek police and the extreme Right syndicalists, but in fact, it was a group of anarchists that had attacked the Right syndicalists and the police had to intervene to end the clashes.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Three of Greece's most famous hotels located on Syntagma Square were forced to evacuate their guests and personnel in view of the uncontrollable situation, something that the media say has not happened since the <a href="/wiki/Dekemvriana" title="Dekemvriana">events of December 1944</a>, which started the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War" title="Greek Civil War">Greek Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_30_June_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_30_June-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, a crowd of people had blocked a number of important political and religious figures from exiting the grounds of the <a href="/wiki/Papafeio" class="mw-redirect" title="Papafeio">Papafeio Orphanage</a>, including Minister of Health <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Loverdos" title="Andreas Loverdos">Andreas Loverdos</a> and the metropolitan bishop of Thessaloniki, Anthimus.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_papafeio_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_papafeio-153">[153]</a></sup> The crowds demanded that the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox Church</a> help Greece in this time of crisis and accused the clergy of receiving oversized salaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_papafeio_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_papafeio-153">[153]</a></sup> When protesters asked the metropolitan bishop how much his religious attire costs, he replied "not much, it's fake".<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_papafeio_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_papafeio-153">[153]</a></sup> They were forced to exit the grounds through the back door with the aid of the police, using police cars and taxis, while Anthimus left on foot.<sup id="cite_ref-Makedonia_papafeio_153-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makedonia_papafeio-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the violent protests and use of tear gas by police to evacuate Syntagma Square the previous evening, peaceful protests continued on 30 June with thousands of people gathered in front of the Greek parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_30_June_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_30_June-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_30_June_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_30_June-154">[154]</a></sup> Demonstrations also took place in Greece's second city, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Agelioforos_30_June_2_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agelioforos_30_June_2-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
