<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="July">July</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: July">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Protests across the country continued in July, marking 5 weeks and 2 days of protest on 1 July. Despite the fact that the austerity measures had been passed, a large crowd, but smaller than on previous days, gathered in front of the Greek parliament to protest peacefully on 2 July.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_2_July_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_2_July-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="August">August</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: August">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The sit-in at <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>'s <a href="/wiki/White_Tower_of_Thessaloniki" title="White Tower of Thessaloniki">White Tower</a> Square held throughout July and early August, until the municipal police evacuated the square of all protesters that had camped inside on 7 August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou-15">[15]</a></sup> The police said that the protesters were in violation of various archaeological and environmental provisions,<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou-15">[15]</a></sup> while also making 7 arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_7_Avgoustou-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 August 2011, the indignants at <a href="/wiki/Heraklion" title="Heraklion">Heraklion</a>'s Eleftherias Square agreed to leave the square peacefully,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_14_August_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_14_August-157">[157]</a></sup> following the intervention of a local prosecutor;<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_14_August_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_14_August-157">[157]</a></sup> the prosecutor had warned that unless the demonstrators evacuate the square force would be used like in Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_14_August_157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_14_August-157">[157]</a></sup> Following the evacuation of the square by the indignants, police cleared the square of the kiosk that the demonstrators had set up.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_14_August_157-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_14_August-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_reactions">Political reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Political reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In an interview for the Greek newspaper <i>Ethnos</i> on 29 May 2011, the vice-president of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Greece" title="Government of Greece">Greek government</a>, Theodoros Pangalos, against whom various slogans had been shouted during the demonstrations, adopted an ironic stance towards the movement. He said that "the formation of a political movement, however much the people who follow the technological trends don't want to hear this, does not depend on how many 'likes' or 'dislikes' it gets on Facebook".<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_29_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_29-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_29_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_29-160">[160]</a></sup> He added that "movements without ideology and organization, that is to say movements based on anger, can only lead to either an ineffective release [of tension], which at the end of the day is of no interest to the political world, or pave the way for an undemocratic change of regime by organized minorities".<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_29_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_29-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_29_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_29-160">[160]</a></sup> In response, the demonstrations addressed many chants to the vice-president, like "the country is sinking, Theodore, lose some weight!" and other more vulgar ones.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnos_29_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnos_29-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_29_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_29-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 May, the spokesman of the Greek government, <a href="/wiki/Giorgos_Petalotis" class="mw-redirect" title="Giorgos Petalotis">Giorgos Petalotis</a>, spoke out against Pangalos, saying that Pangalos should remember that when he took part in demonstrations against the dictatorship as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party</a> in 1973, "some people considered these demonstrations provocative".<sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Petalotis_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Petalotis-161">[161]</a></sup> He furthermore added that not only does the Indignant Citizens Movement have a clear ideology (even if it is a "technology trend" as Pangalos described it), but that it also "reflects the real needs of the Greek society".<sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Petalotis_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Petalotis-161">[161]</a></sup> He pointed out that "denial [of the system] and no proposals lead nowhere".<sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Petalotis_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Petalotis-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 June, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Greece" title="Prime Minister of Greece">Prime Minister of Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">George Papandreou</a>, commented in regards to the Indignant Citizens Movement saying that "today protesters in Greece and the world are demonstrating against matters of national governance which are more weak than they used to be and, despite their inner weaknesses, are trapped by the global powers and the changes of a global system".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Papandreou_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Papandreou-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the blockade of the Parliament by angry citizens on 31 May, which prevented the MPs inside from exiting the building, and also after the angry reactions against the MPs when they were allowed to exit (such as the throwing of empty water bottles, fruit and other objects), the deputy Minister of Education said "I understand that the Indignant Citizens Movement is not a threat to democracy, but violence is, and I condemn it".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Antidraseis_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Antidraseis-163">[163]</a></sup> She added that "in a democracy, violence should be prevented and not tolerated" and that "the majority of the MPs in parliament are young; they should receive the same treatment as old MPs".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Antidraseis_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Antidraseis-163">[163]</a></sup> The deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs commented that "I can accept tougher questioning and criticism, but not the leveling of our political system. Democracy can give [a] solution. The flattening of our democracy can only lead to a slippery road. The majority of the Greek people can be angry, but not under these circumstances".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Antidraseis_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Antidraseis-163">[163]</a></sup></p>

</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2gwF8J2N2BM"><span class="plainlinks">The protests of Thessaloniki on 25 May</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a></td>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S20_JuaX8gg"><span class="plainlinks">Video of police brutality on 29 June, destroying tents and hitting civilians</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=p5FARBm7k48"><span class="plainlinks">Video of police hitting and gassing people in a grocery store near Syntagma on 29 June</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128" /> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2xR_ME-XYZM"><span class="plainlinks">Video of police throwing tear gas inside a Metro station packed with people</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">European Parliament MP</a> Theodoros Skylakakis, who is aligned with the newly founded <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(Greece)" title="Democratic Alliance (Greece)">Democratic Alliance</a> party, said that "these people need to get a sense of political ideology and move to a deeper revelation: from what they don't like, to what they like",<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_29_2_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_29_2-164">[164]</a></sup> implying that a non-political movement will be ineffective and without results. <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Tsipras" title="Alexis Tsipras">Alexis Tsipras</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Synaspismos" title="Synaspismos">Synaspismos</a> radical left party and the first party leader to comment on the demonstrations, said that "no one has the right to make the people [silent], or tell them that they have no say in their country's future by means of a referendum".<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Tsipras_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Tsipras-165">[165]</a></sup> He added that the <a href="/wiki/Left_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Left (politics)">Left</a> should be supportive of the demonstrations and that "things are turning at a fast pace, and the people are waking up".<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Tsipras_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Tsipras-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Athens" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Athens">Mayor of Athens</a> said on 30 May that the protest was a "healthy and sound demonstration", but when a motion was put forth at the municipal council to declare the municipality's support for the demonstrations, the mayor said that he felt "it is not appropriate to express our sympathy".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_6i_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_6i-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with a Greek newspaper on 1 June 2011, the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Democracia_real_Ya" class="mw-redirect" title="Democracia real Ya">Democracia real Ya</a>! movement, which organised the <a href="/wiki/2011_Spanish_Protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Spanish Protests">2011 Spanish Protests</a> and sparked the Greek protests, said that its members support the Greek demonstrations and that "this is only the beginning".<sup id="cite_ref-Proto_Thema_Democracia_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proto_Thema_Democracia-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 June 2011, 16 parliament members of PASOK publicly demanded of <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">George Papandreou</a> that the parliament make a full report of country's current financial situation.<sup id="cite_ref-.CE.A4.CE.BF_.CE.92.CE.AE.CE.BC.CE.B1_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.CE.A4.CE.BF_.CE.92.CE.AE.CE.BC.CE.B1-167">[167]</a></sup> This was caused by the forthcoming second memoradum voting, which <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">George Papandreou</a> characterised as "urgent".</p>
<p>In the early hours of 22 June 2011, George Papandreou and his government narrowly survived a <a href="/wiki/Vote_of_confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Vote of confidence">vote of confidence</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greek_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek parliament">Greek parliament</a>, with 155 of the 300 seats voting in favour.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_confidence_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_confidence-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 June 2011, amid violent protests in the square outside parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Hellenic Parliament</a> voted in favour of passing a new set of <a href="/wiki/Austerity_measures" class="mw-redirect" title="Austerity measures">austerity measures</a> with a marginal majority of 155 seats in the 300-seat parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Mesoprothesmo_30_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Mesoprothesmo_30-169">[169]</a></sup> The measures themselves had attracted much criticism both from the Greek public and within the country's political scene. Between June and July 2011, <a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Socialist_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Panhellenic Socialist Movement">Panhellenic Socialist Movement</a> (PASOK) went from an 156-seat majority to a 154-seat one, while <a href="/wiki/New_Democracy_(Greece)" title="New Democracy (Greece)">New Democracy</a> also lost one seat.</p>
<p>The allegations of <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> by Greek and foreign media<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_police_brutality_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_police_brutality-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_police_brutality_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_police_brutality-18">[18]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a><sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_police_brutality_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International_police_brutality-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_police_brutality2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International_police_brutality2-21">[21]</a></sup> sparked heated debate in the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Parliament" title="Hellenic Parliament">Hellenic Parliament</a>, with all parties in the house asking the government for explanations, including MPs of the ruling PASOK party.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> The leader of the opposition, <a href="/wiki/Antonis_Samaras" title="Antonis Samaras">Antonis Samaras</a>, characterised the situation as almost that of a "parastate",<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/George_Karatzaferis" class="mw-redirect" title="George Karatzaferis">George Karatzaferis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Orthodox_Rally" title="Popular Orthodox Rally">Popular Orthodox Rally</a> accused the government of "not being able to control 200 thugs in central Athens".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Radical_Left" class="mw-redirect" title="Coalition of the Radical Left">Coalition of the Radical Left</a> party accused the government of "abolishing the very principles of democracy"<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> and filed a complaint against the government for "cheering while at the same time outside the building tear gas was being overly used".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> Members of the parliamentary group of PASOK characterised the actions of the police as "barbaric"<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christos_Papoutsis" title="Christos Papoutsis">Christos Papoutsis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Citizen_Protection" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Citizen Protection">Minister for Citizen Protection</a>, denied all accusations claiming that "it's the police that operates, not the government".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> Regarding the video in which police are allegedly helping hooded youth, he said that the people in the video are not police;<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> the Athens Prosecutor accepted the demands for an investigation into the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Paremvasi_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Paremvasi-24">[24]</a></sup> On the matter of the attack on the <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Syntagma station">Sytagma Square metro station</a> using tear gas by police, the minister said that "people with health issues were transported to hospitals and the others left inside were wearing gas masks more expensive than the ones used by police".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Giannis_Ragousis" title="Giannis Ragousis">Giannis Ragousis</a>, Minister for Transport, asked for a disciplinary measure to punish those responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> stated that any use of violence is sad and unacceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Askos_Aiolou_170-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Askos_Aiolou-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally, the Greek government has pledged to amend the constitution as a result of the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathimerini_referendum_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathimerini_referendum-171">[171]</a></sup> Among the most important aspects of the constitutional reform will be the change of the functions of the Greek political system.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathimerini_referendum_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathimerini_referendum-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Government_reform_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Government_reform-172">[172]</a></sup> The Greek government has said it will open up the discussion on constitutional amendment in September, both to the public and the media.<sup id="cite_ref-Government_reform_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Government_reform-172">[172]</a></sup> Other media have pointed out that this could not be legal before 2013 because the <a href="/wiki/Greek_constitutional_amendment_of_2008" title="Greek constitutional amendment of 2008">constitutional amendment of 2008</a> forbids any other changes to the constitution prior to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Kathimerini_referendum_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kathimerini_referendum-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_perception_and_media_coverage">Public perception and media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Public perception and media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In a survey published in June 2011 by Public Issue on behalf of the Greek TV channel <a href="/wiki/Skai_TV" title="Skai TV">Skai</a>, 98% of people asked said they were informed about the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> Additionally, 95% of people asked said they had positive impressions about the movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> When asked about their overall opinion of the movement, 86% replied either positive (76%) or probably positive (10%) while 6% replied negative, with an additional 2% as probably negative.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> 35% of the people asked said they had participated in at least one protest.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> When asked about their opinion in regards to the media coverage of the events, 53% replied negative and 39% positive.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> 51% thought the demonstrations are a "very important" event, while 34% felt it was "quite important", with 12% replying they viewed it as either not very important or not important at all.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> When asked if they believe that the protests may have been politically orchestrated by a political power within the country, 80% replied no and 16% yes.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup> Finally, 52% believed that the protests will bring results, while 39% believed they will not.<sup id="cite_ref-Public_Issue_PDF_173-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Public_Issue_PDF-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>Demonstrations were scheduled to continue for "as long as it takes".<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Proti_Grammi_27-105">[105]</a></sup> These demonstrations were the largest event to be organised over the internet in Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-ERT_2_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERT_2-174">[174]</a></sup> With the exception of <a href="/wiki/Skai_TV" title="Skai TV">Skai TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_Channel" title="Star Channel">Star Channel</a> and Zougla Radio, which provided live coverage of the demonstrations in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, media coverage of these events was relatively poor in the first weeks. Major Greek TV channel <a href="/wiki/Mega_Channel" title="Mega Channel">Mega</a> was forced to temporarily deactivate its Facebook page as thousands of people left negative and derogatory comments on the page because the channel did not cover the events of 29 May.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_31_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_31-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mega_Facebook_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mega_Facebook-175">[175]</a></sup> The demonstrations did catch the attention of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, and the spokesman of the organisation expressed "understanding" for the demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_27_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_27-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMF_27_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_27-177">[177]</a></sup> Additionally, the demonstrations have also been featured in <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">El País</a></i>, <i>El Economista</i> and <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_100.2C000_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_100.2C000-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Euronews_25_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euronews_25-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-El_Pa.C3.ADs_25_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Pa.C3.ADs_25-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-El_Economista_25_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El_Economista_25-180">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mikis_Theodorakis" title="Mikis Theodorakis">Mikis Theodorakis</a>, prominent Greek songwriter and political activist, especially during the years of the dictatorship (1967–1974), also expressed his support for the movement in an open letter addressed to the demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_28_2_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_28_2-181">[181]</a></sup> Famous Greek singer Giannis Kotsiras also expressed his open support for the initiative. Some members of the Greek clergy have also expressed their open support for the demonstrations, notably bishops Anthimus of Thessaloniki and Ambrosius of <a href="/wiki/Kalavryta" title="Kalavryta">Kalavryta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Ambrosios_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Ambrosios-182">[182]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_protests_in_2011">Other protests in 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other protests in 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="August_2">August</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: August">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 23 August 2011, there was a demonstration by workers in the tourism sector. The Pan-Worker's Front staged a <a href="/wiki/Sit-in" title="Sit-in">sit-in</a> at some of Athens' most famous hotels on <a href="/wiki/Syntagma_Square" title="Syntagma Square">Syntagma Square</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Varea_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Varea-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Synexizetai_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Synexizetai-184">[184]</a></sup> as well as the iconic Electra Palace Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aristotelous_Square" title="Aristotelous Square">Aristotelous Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Varea_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Varea-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Synexizetai_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Synexizetai-184">[184]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Federation of Tourism Workers held a 24-hour strike and a demonstration in a central square of Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Varea_183-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Varea-183">[183]</a></sup> The Federation also said that they would hold another 24-hour strike, but did not define a date for it.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Varea_183-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Varea-183">[183]</a></sup> The sit-in at various hotels was met with criticism from government officials as well as various labour unions involved in the tourism sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Varea_183-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Varea-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Synexizetai_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Synexizetai-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="September">September</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: September">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early September 2011, as new measures were announced by the Minister for Finance on 6 September,<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Venizelos_Troika_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Venizelos_Troika-185">[185]</a></sup> various unions of the country's public sector announced they would go on strike.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Baraz_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Baraz-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Pyretos_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Pyretos-187">[187]</a></sup> These include teachers, doctors, taxi drivers, customs officials and tax collectors,<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Eforiakoi_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Eforiakoi-188">[188]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Waste_collector" title="Waste collector">waste collectors</a> working for the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Baraz_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Baraz-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Pyretos_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Pyretos-187">[187]</a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_controller" title="Air traffic controller">air traffic controller</a>'s union announced that, in the interest of serving the public, air traffic controllers would not go on strike but would refuse to work overtime.<sup id="cite_ref-Eleftherotypia_Enaeria_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eleftherotypia_Enaeria-189">[189]</a></sup> Workers at the Swedens Urban Transport Organization (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Athens_Metro" title="Athens Metro">Athens Metro</a>) are considering going on strike as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Ta_Nea_Pyretos_187-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ta_Nea_Pyretos-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="October">October</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: October">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 5 October 2011, there was a general strike.<sup id="cite_ref-October_BBC_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_BBC-190">[190]</a></sup> During the demonstrations police clashed with youth and made 10 arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-October_Skai_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_Skai-191">[191]</a></sup> Police are also investigating claims by journalists that they were assaulted by police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-October_Skai_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_Skai-191">[191]</a></sup> The police officer who assaulted the journalist was arrested, but then released on 6 October until conclusive evidence is found.<sup id="cite_ref-October_Skai_2_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_Skai_2-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were demonstrations in co-ordination with the <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> movement on <a href="/wiki/15_October_2011_global_protests" title="15 October 2011 global protests">15 October</a>. Only 7,000 demonstrators, according to estimates by local media, gathered on Syntagma square in a peaceful demonstration.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Further protests and strikes were organised for 19 and 20 October.</p>
<p>The strikes in fact began on 17 October, when the seaman's union walked off the job for 48 hours,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> shutting down the ferry services between the islands. Customs officials who clear fuel refinery deliveries also held a 24-hour strike that day. The shortage of fuel and goods in the Greek islands due to the strike of ferry and fuel services has already begun to manifest itself.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Trofima_Venzini_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Trofima_Venzini-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second day of the protests was marked by clashes between members of <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Greece" title="Communist Party of Greece">Communist Party</a> (KKE) and hard-line protestors (mainly <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Greece" title="Anarchism in Greece">anarchists</a>) who tried to invade the parliament, resulting in the death of one KKE member.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 October (a national holiday <a href="/wiki/Ochi_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Ochi Day">in Greece</a>), protests occurred nationwide. In <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, where a national military parade is held annually, protesters prevented the parade from officially taking place<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki-197">[197]</a></sup> (the first time this occurred since the parade was first held in 1941) and shouted slogans against <a href="/wiki/Karolos_Papoulias" title="Karolos Papoulias">Karolos Papoulias</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki-197">[197]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Greece" title="President of Greece">President of Greece</a>, who was forced to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki_197-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Thessaloniki-197">[197]</a></sup> However, the civilian part of the parade along with the conscriptees marched as planned, acclaimed by the crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> In Athens, during the annual student parade, several schools turned their heads away from the officials present (which included <a href="/wiki/Anna_Diamantopoulou" title="Anna Diamantopoulou">Anna Diamantopoulou</a>, the Minister of Education),<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Athina_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Athina-199">[199]</a></sup> while of the members of the band of the Municipality of Athens attached black ribbons to their instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Athina_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Athina-199">[199]</a></sup> Additionally, a crowd of people had gathered in front of Hotel Grand Bretagne in central Athens (close to the VIP stand) and shouted slogans against the economic crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Athina_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Athina-199">[199]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Heraklion" title="Heraklion">Heraklion</a> protesters threw eggs at the officials,<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Kriti_Patra_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Kriti_Patra-200">[200]</a></sup> while in <a href="/wiki/Patras" title="Patras">Patras</a> protesters occupied the street where the scheduled student parade was to take place and shouted slogans against the officials present (which included the Minister for Defence).<sup id="cite_ref-Skai_Parelasi_Kriti_Patra_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skai_Parelasi_Kriti_Patra-200">[200]</a></sup> Heckling of politicians occurred in many other cities across the country, including <a href="/wiki/Trikala" title="Trikala">Trikala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volos" title="Volos">Volos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serres" title="Serres">Serres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veroia" class="mw-redirect" title="Veroia">Veroia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tripoli_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripoli (Greece)">Tripoli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="November">November</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: November">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 17 November, as part of the ongoing protests that led to the resignation of the <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">Papandreau</a> government, over 50 thousand people marched in Athens<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="December">December</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: December">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 6 December, to mark an anniversary of the death of <a href="/wiki/Alexandros_Grigoropoulos" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexandros Grigoropoulos">Alexandros Grigoropoulos</a>, thousands of people marched on the Parliament building, throwing <a href="/wiki/Molotov_Cocktail" class="mw-redirect" title="Molotov Cocktail">Molotov Cocktails</a> at the police, who responded with tear gas.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_protests">2012 protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-austerity_movement_in_Greece&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2012 protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 12 February, as many as 500,000 protesters gathered in Athens outside the Parliament House to voice opposition to <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Papademos" title="Lucas Papademos">Lucas Papademos</a>' caretaker cabinet's austerity measures which were being debated in Parliament. The passing of the austerity measures is a precondition for the next €130 billion lending package from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> to the Greek government, without which the country would face <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_default" title="Sovereign default">sovereign default</a> by 20 March. Police used large amounts of tear gas and flash grenades, while protesters hurled stones and <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktails</a>. In total 45 buildings were set ablaze and 25 protesters and 40 officers were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn2012_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2012-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> The protests had been preceded by a 24-hour nationwide general strike on 7 February, when the two largest labour unions in Greece said the proposed measures would "drive Greek society to despair."<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>Speaking to members of Parliament, Papademos called for calm and urged members to pass the plan while asserting that violence and vandalism had no place in democracy. He also stated to the lawmakers that if the majority of them chose to vote against the austerity measures there would be several onerous consequences, including that the government would not be able to pay the salaries of its employees. On 13 February, the Greek Parliament subsequently approved this latest round of austerity measures by a vote of 199 to 74.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn2012_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2012-204">[204]</a></sup> On 20 March, the government finally announced they have defaulted and rejected another package from Brussels Bailout and are starting to reform the system.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> On 5 April, people once again demonstrated against the government after a pensioner named <a href="/wiki/Dimitris_Christoulas" title="Dimitris Christoulas">Dimitris Christoulas</a> committed suicide by shooting himself, refusing to share the fate of those people who have had to search for food in garbage.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 October 2012 another demonstration against austerity measures was held. During the demonstration, clashes broke out and a man died of heart attack outside the parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
